  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b595b12f-5b76-4019-ae97-f976b29c33f5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText15733639430469463566" style="display:none">GROUNDHOG DAY meets FLIPPED in this tale of a girl stuck in her birthday.<br /><br />It's Amanda's 11th birthday and she is super excited -- after all, 11 is so different from 10. But from the start, everything goes wrong. The worst part of it all is that she and her best friend, Leo, with whom she's shared every birthday, are on the outs and this will be the first birthday they haven't shared together. When Amanda turns in for the night, glad to have her birthday behind her, she wakes up happy for a new day. Or is it? Her birthday seems to be repeating iself. What is going on?! And how can she fix it? Only time, friendship, and a little luck will tell. . .</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43550889?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43550889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1176667160548221156">Reviewed by Allison Fraclose for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>On the day that Amanda Ellerby and Leo Fitzpatrick were born, a mysterious woman with a birthmark shaped like a duck told their parents that the two newborns would grow up to be the best of friends, and that they should always celebrate their birthdays together. <br/><br/>Through a fluke, one year later, both sets of parents booked the same location for their child's first birthday, and Amanda and Leo took to each other so much that celebrating their birthd</span>
  <span id="freeText1176667160548221156" style="display:none">Reviewed by Allison Fraclose for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />On the day that Amanda Ellerby and Leo Fitzpatrick were born, a mysterious woman with a birthmark shaped like a duck told their parents that the two newborns would grow up to be the best of friends, and that they should always celebrate their birthdays together. <br /><br />Through a fluke, one year later, both sets of parents booked the same location for their child's first birthday, and Amanda and Leo took to each other so much that celebrating their birthday together in the small town of Willow Falls became a great town tradition. <br /><br />Ten years later, Amanda Ellerby is absolutely dreading her eleventh birthday party, the first that she will spend without her ex-friend, Leo. She hasn't spoken to him in exactly one year, ever since she heard him say those nasty things about her at their last joint birthday party. <br /><br />What's worse is that she's heard all these rumors about the incredible party Leo's parents are throwing for him--with a hypnotist, a band, and a real football player--while she's stuck with this costume party idea that her own mom came up with. <br /><br />The day finally arrives, and Amanda's eleventh birthday ends up even worse than she could have imagined. She has a pop quiz in History, she bombs the gymnastics tryouts, and only a few people show up at her party (some kids even leave to go to Leo's party instead). When she finally takes off her itchy Dorothy costume with the blistering shoes and crawls into bed, she feels nothing but relief that this horrible day is over. <br /><br />Except that it isn't. The next day is her birthday again. And the day after that. And the day after that. Is Amanda the only one stuck in this terrible time loop? <br /><br />I absolutely fell in love with this sweet tale of friendship, magic, and old rivalries. A quickly moving story with some unforgettable characters, 11 BIRTHDAYS takes that Groundhog Day premise and turns it into something much more meaningful. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1176667160548221156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14605038661025039346"><blockquote>
  <b>"Then put your little hand in mine. There ain't no hill or mountain we can't climb..."</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I remember watching <i>Groundhog Day</i> over and over again when I was younger. That scene when the alarm clock would chime Sunny and Cher at 6:00 on the dot always cracked me up. The possibilities of reliving the same day without any repercussions was such an amazing concept. <br/><br/>That is a major segment of <i>11 Birthdays</i>'s premise. Amanda and her best friend Leo, live in a charming, magical town called Willow Falls. O</span>
  <span id="freeText14605038661025039346" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>"Then put your little hand in mine. There ain't no hill or mountain we can't climb..."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I remember watching <i>Groundhog Day</i> over and over again when I was younger. That scene when the alarm clock would chime Sunny and Cher at 6:00 on the dot always cracked me up. The possibilities of reliving the same day without any repercussions was such an amazing concept. <br /><br />That is a major segment of <i>11 Birthdays</i>'s premise. Amanda and her best friend Leo, live in a charming, magical town called Willow Falls. On the day of her 11th birthday, things don't quite work out like she expects. Like <i>Sixteen Candles</i>, everything that could possibly go wrong does! When that day keeps happening over and over again, Amanda decides to decipher the mystery behind the enchantment.<br /><br />I listened to the audio version of the book and I just loved Kathleen McInerney's narration. It's not easy making an 11-year-old girl's voice believable, plus all the other characters. I'm looking forward to continuing the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14605038661025039346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72560438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer233393377312528064">3 1/2 stars. Genres are intertwined here--realistic fiction with a twist of fantasy. Leo and Amanda, born on the same day, have celebrated every birthday together until this year—their 11th. The two had a falling out during their 10th birthday celebration and they have not spoken for a year. Separate birthday parties are planned for the first time in their lives, but then weird things start to happen. Amanda and Leo get stuck in time and their 11th birthday keeps repeating until…<br/><br/>A quick read tha</span>
  <span id="freeText233393377312528064" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars. Genres are intertwined here--realistic fiction with a twist of fantasy. Leo and Amanda, born on the same day, have celebrated every birthday together until this year—their 11th. The two had a falling out during their 10th birthday celebration and they have not spoken for a year. Separate birthday parties are planned for the first time in their lives, but then weird things start to happen. Amanda and Leo get stuck in time and their 11th birthday keeps repeating until…<br /><br />A quick read that I think kids might like. The characters are well-developed. I think the author nails 5th grade relationships. I have a few quibbles with some details in the book. And Leo’s dialog sometimes sounds like a 21-year-old instead of an 11-year-old. I felt the story dragged a bit in places, but overall a fun read.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17810353617589650975"><a href='http://www.goodreadingguide.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/>Wendy Mass writes highly enjoyable realistic fiction with a fantasy twist. The characters are well developed and the 11-year-old friendships and dramas are true to life.<br/><br/>There’s a great message about the need to resolve disagreements and heal grudges—even among 11-year-olds—before you can move on. The story has the poignancy of that 90s movie ‘Groundhog Day’, for a much younger audience.<br/><br/>For girls who need a friendship story this is a fun, easy read.</span>

<div id="review_42612299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42612299" />
    <a title="nan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1888755-nan"><img alt="nan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242172703p2/1888755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42612299?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nan" href="/user/show/1888755-nan">nan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42612299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18049444244533096697">I gave this book four stars, which is a lot for me. i tend to rate low. It's about a girl who was born on the same day as this boy, and they have always celebrated their birthdays together for years. This year (turning 11) they have a fight and don't. The day after their birthday, it is their birthday again. and again. and again. Sounds kind of weird, but i really liked it!!!</span>

<div id="review_509313671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/509313671" />
    <a title="Maddie D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13857996-maddie-d"><img alt="Maddie D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360102682p2/13857996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/509313671?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie D" href="/user/show/13857996-maddie-d">Maddie D</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer509313671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3863692684052954717">1/17/13<br/><br/>I am currently reading 11 birthdays by Wendy Mass. This book is about a girl named Amanda and a boy named Leo. They always have their birthdays together. But from what happened at Amanda's and Leo's 10th birthday, they're definitely not having their 11th birthday together. While Amanda is trying to plan her party she is also trying to get her back handspring down to make gymnastics tryouts. But her best friend Stephanie is putting way to much pressure on her to make the gymnastics team. B</span>
  <span id="freeText3863692684052954717" style="display:none">1/17/13<br /><br />I am currently reading 11 birthdays by Wendy Mass. This book is about a girl named Amanda and a boy named Leo. They always have their birthdays together. But from what happened at Amanda's and Leo's 10th birthday, they're definitely not having their 11th birthday together. While Amanda is trying to plan her party she is also trying to get her back handspring down to make gymnastics tryouts. But her best friend Stephanie is putting way to much pressure on her to make the gymnastics team. But Amanda loves playing the drums and band tryouts are the same time as gymnastics tryouts. So far I think this book has been great! For example it's really fun to read because Amanda's birthday is so different with out Leo being there. And she's trying to make the gymnastics try outs the same time day as her birthday, and the same time as band tryouts is going on. This book can relate to me because I was trying to get my back handspring down for a gymnastics team also. But I was also trying to try out for soccer. I was getting a lot of pressure on me because I didn't know if I should tryout for gymnastics or soccer. I ended up choosing soccer because I like doing it more and I'm better at it. I'm so much like Amanda in various ways. Another way is that Amanda's best friend Stephanie, is hanging out with another friend named Ruby, way more than Amanda. My friend has done that to me also. Like I said, this book can just relate to me in so many ways which is why I like this book so much.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />2/5/13<br />I am still reading 11 birthdays by Wendy Mass. As I keep reading this book it just keeps getting better and better. A reason for why I believe this is because Amanda's and Leo's 11th happens over and over again. The day just keeps repeating! Its very funny to read things that happen in this book because the choices that Amanda and Leo make practically change the whole day. For example one day Amanda and Leo skip school and try to figure out how the day is repeating. Well they lost track of time. Once their parents found them at the mall, they got in huge trouble! But of course it didn't matter because the next day was like a do over day. This is definitely a character driven book because its about Amanda and Leo trying to figure out why their 11th birthday is repeating. This book relates to me because I have soccer practice 4 times a week and a lot of the times we do the same things so it feels like the day is repeating. Which is like Amanda's and Leo's birthday repeating. Overall this book is great and I think people who like fiction should read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3863692684052954717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81480853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81480853" />
    <a title="Student" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3053706-student"><img alt="Student" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81480853?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Student" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Student" href="/user/show/3053706-student">Student</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer81480853&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81480853" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12265567634013904407">Review by: Tessa McCorkell<br/> <br/>11 Birthdays<br/> <br/>1. What did you think the book was about?<br/>This book is about forgiveness, friendship and traditions. Leo fitzpatrick and Amanda Ellerby were born on the same day and celebrate it together every year. But on their 10th they got into a fight that lasted a whole year. When a curse is thrust upon them they must work out their differences and find a way out!<br/> <br/>2. Did you feel that the book fulfilled your expectations? Were you disappointed?<br/>It definitely fulfilled </span>
  <span id="freeText12265567634013904407" style="display:none">Review by: Tessa McCorkell<br /> <br />11 Birthdays<br /> <br />1. What did you think the book was about?<br />This book is about forgiveness, friendship and traditions. Leo fitzpatrick and Amanda Ellerby were born on the same day and celebrate it together every year. But on their 10th they got into a fight that lasted a whole year. When a curse is thrust upon them they must work out their differences and find a way out!<br /> <br />2. Did you feel that the book fulfilled your expectations? Were you disappointed?<br />It definitely fulfilled my expectations. This may have been the best book I have ever read. It’s filled with laughs, tears, sighs and smiles. It keeps you entertained the whole time.” Leo recites a few lines about friendship and birthdays_ ‘I thought you don’t red your poetry in front of people.’ ‘I don’t I mean I haven’t before but that’s what today is all about.’”<br /> <br />3. What about the plot did it pull you in; or did you have to force yourself to read the book.<br />11 Birthdays is a book with realistic and fictional scenes. The plot is 2 former best friends who share the same birthday but their 11th keeps repeating itself over and over until Leo and Amanda work out the solution.” don’t you see? They ignored the old woman’s warning and keep fighting, then after the one year mark passed, they got stuck in the loop. You and me got into a fight last year on our birthday, so this year on our birthday the enchantment or what ever it was kicked in. I guess its ‘cause were related.<br /> <br />4. Were the characters realistic? Would you want to meet any of the characters? Did you like them? Hate them?<br />I really wanted to meet one of the main characters Leo. He seemed like a really nice, funny, generous and fun person to be around. He was comforting to listen to throughout the book. “If I had to be stuck in time with any one I’m glad it’s you.”<br /> <br />5. If one (or more) of the characters made a choice that had moral implications, would you have made the same decision? Why? Why not?<br />If Leo or Amanda had decided not to work together to find a way to stop the “dreadful Friday” from repeating their whole life, I don’t think I would have liked this book as much. I loved their best friend relationship and wishes I had one as strong as theirs.<br /> <br />6. How would the book have been different if it had taken place in a different place or time?<br />If 11 birthdays had taken place in a different time in Leo and Amanda’s lives like when they were younger they would not have understood the whole situation “Imagine yourselves stuck in this situation before you were even six years old” Or in the past like 100 years ago the=is whole situation may not have been even imaginable.<br /> <br />7. What are some of the book’s themes? Were they important?<br />Some of the books themes are friendship, forgiveness and traditions. Leo and Amanda were best friends since birth. Their parents met in the hospital “which ones yours?” That one “she said pointing to the little girl who was rubbing her eyes. “She’s precious” then she pointed to the boy who was now happily sucking his fist. “That ones ours”<br /><br />8. Did the book end the way you expected it to?<br />11 birthdays ended on a happy note as I expected it to. It was pretty predictable that they would find a way out of the enchantment or at least stop it for the time being. But I had no idea how they would free themselves.<br /><br />9. Would you recommend this book to other readers? To your close friends?<br />This book was great I would recommend it to anyone who is up for a short, funny, entertaining read.” it’s like we get a do-over everyday!” Imagine the possibilities if every reset its self.<br /><br />10. What was your favorite part /scene of the book?<br />My favorite scene of the book was when Amanda and Leo “finally made up.” It was really toughing because you could see how good of friends they used to be and it’s really too bad when you see great friends get into fights. So when they made up, I guess you could say it gave me hope to become better friends with my old friends I haven’t talked to in a while.<br /><br />11. What was your least favorite part/ scene of the book?<br />My least favorite part of the book would have to be when Leo and Amanda got caught skipping class at the mall. I knew from the description of the characters that they were really good people and would normally never skip. They got into a lot of trouble for doing that and were both stuck in their rooms all night.<br /><br />12. How are the book’s images symbolically significant? Do the images help to develop the plot, or help define the characters?<br />There weren’t any images in the book but there was symbolism Amanda and Leo decorated flower pots for their 5th birthday and an old woman with a duck shaped birth mark “gave Amanda a seed from Leos great great grandfathers tree and gave Leo a seed from Amanda’s great great grandfather’s tree” This was supposed to keep off the enchantment till they were 18 years old as long as they kept their trees near. But after the fight on their 10th birthday Amanda “tossed the pot out the window” into a nearby hedge. Could it still be there?<br /><br />13. Were there any personality traits in the character that you could identify with?<br />I was a lot like Amanda when I was younger I was a bit of a tomboy, my best friends were guys because I found it hard to always get along with girls and I could imagine the un imaginable. Amanda had these same traits that were shown throughout the book.<br /><br />14. What did you learn from the book you didn’t already know?<br />11 birthdays was more for our entertaining then to tell us an information. But I guess you could say I learned to think more creatively.” I reach over to shut off my alarm, not even remotely surprised anymore that’s its going off without me setting it” “My backpack is waiting for me downstairs, as I suspected it would be even though I had left it in my locker”pg.187 . These are just a few examples of the crazy lines from the book that you would need a big imagination to understand.<br /><br />15. On a scale from 1-5 what do you rate this book- what would have made this book better?<br />I gave 11 birthdays a 5 stars but I think the characters could have been described in better detail. I pictured Amanda with long wavy brown hair blue eyes and a mix between tomboy and casual style. Leo having short brown hair a big happy smile and casual style. How will you picture them?<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12265567634013904407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/431650501?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="6cayleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="6cayleigh" href="/user/show/13033160-6cayleigh">6cayleigh</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

                    style="display:none"

<span id="freeTextContainer18412827002107910302">What I learned from this book?<br/><br/>I learned you can solve any problem if you put your mind to it.<br/><br/><br/>11 Birthdays is a fiction story about a girl who repeats her eleventh birthday eleven times. The narrator of this book is a girl named Amanda. Everything goes wrong right from the beginning, her best friend Leo and her are in a huge fight and there birthdays are on the same day. On the first day Amanda has a horrible birthday. When she woke up something was not right, she thought her family was playing a</span>
  <span id="freeText18412827002107910302" style="display:none">What I learned from this book?<br><br>I learned you can solve any problem if you put your mind to it.<br><br><br>11 Birthdays is a fiction story about a girl who repeats her eleventh birthday eleven times. The narrator of this book is a girl named Amanda. Everything goes wrong right from the beginning, her best friend Leo and her are in a huge fight and there birthdays are on the same day. On the first day Amanda has a horrible birthday. When she woke up something was not right, she thought her family was playing a joke on her, but then something strange happened. The next day she woke up and it was her eleventh birthday AGAIN! This continued for eleven days. Through out the book she and Leo have to find there way and figure out what is happening. I would recommend this book because it is a mixture of genres, comedy, mystery, and there are quite a bit of cliff hangers. This book is one of my favorite books and one I can read over and over again! <br><br><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4835838.11_Birthdays__11_Birthdays___1_" title="11 Birthdays (11 Birthdays, #1) by Wendy Mass" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer4353228871852710427">I am currently reading the book 11 BIRTHDAYS by Wendy Mass. It's about a girl named Amanda who is having a lot of problems with friendships. Her best friend became her ex-best friend and her new best friend is drifting off to be friends with mean, old Ruby. I've known people like Ruby and they can be pretty viscous but if you get to know them, they might actually be pretty nice. Maybe they're just looking for a friend and the only way they can get one is by stealing it. But if you give them a fr</span>
  <span id="freeText4353228871852710427" style="display:none">I am currently reading the book 11 BIRTHDAYS by Wendy Mass. It's about a girl named Amanda who is having a lot of problems with friendships. Her best friend became her ex-best friend and her new best friend is drifting off to be friends with mean, old Ruby. I've known people like Ruby and they can be pretty viscous but if you get to know them, they might actually be pretty nice. Maybe they're just looking for a friend and the only way they can get one is by stealing it. But if you give them a friend (A.K.A you) they can be nice. I haven't gotten to far in the book (about page 50) so I'm not sure that that's what Amanda's gonna do. I do know that it's her 11th birthday and it's been pretty lousy. And tomorrow won't be any better (hint, hint). I'm not sure why the day will repeat, but I think it has something to do with her and Leo (Amanda's ex-best friend) having separate birthdays. I have my theories about what's gonna happen, but I won't say anything. I love the way that Mass brings Amanda to life and puts the reader straight into Amanda's head. When I'm reading this book it feels like everything has disappeared and I'm right there with Amanda in Willow Falls. Overall I give this book 5 stars. And if you read it, I hope you agree.<br /><br /><br /> ~Lexi Z.<br />_____________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________<br /><br />I recently finished the book 11 BIRTHDAYS by Wendy Mass. It's about a girl named Amanda who has a really bad day and is ready for it to end. But hen she wakes up Saturday morning, it's Friday again!!!! And of all the people that she could be going through this day loop with, it's her ex best friend Leo. Though this book is funny, adventurous, suspenseful, and mysterious, I hint it also has a message. Friends make mistakes sometimes. Say mean things, do mean things, ignore you for a little while. But sometimes they don't mean it. They don't realize what they're doing is mean or that you're feeling excluded. If you don't forgive them for their mistakes, it my mess you up for a while. (No as bad as Leo and Amanda, but you know what I mean.) I define toy learned from this book. Friends ARE important. I think this book is issue oriented because they have to deal with the day loop and the mistakes that they made during some of the days. My eleventh birthday wasn't quite as eventful as Leo and Amanda's (they share a birthday), but I wish it had been because that would give me something REALLY interesting about myself. My rating of this book isn't the same. It's time I give it 10 stars, and his time I know you'll agree.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer600048558151063391">Summary: In the book 11 Birthdays by Wendy Mass the two main characters Amanda and Leo get into a fight.   <span id="freeText600048558151063391" style="display:none">Summary: In the book 11 Birthdays by Wendy Mass the two main characters Amanda and Leo get into a fight. They have had their birthday every year since they were little but since they are in a fight they don't this year. The day of Amanda and Leo's birthday they don't go so great so they just tag along that day and they don't really care. When they wake up the next day they both realize that everything is exactly the same as yesterday. Amanda knew the days were repeating but didn't know how and she thought she was the only one that knew the days were repeating. Until she noticed Leo was acting different than "the day before". They had to get back together and figure out together how to stop the day from repeating. With a little bit of arguments, getting in trouble, and trespassing, they figured out how the days were repeating and they figured out they just needed to become good friends again.<br /><br />recommendation: I recommend this book to people because in the book even though the two main characters get in a fight it shows that you can get over it and become friends with someone because its bad to give up on someone. Another recommendation why you should read this book is because it explains the setting very well, and you can picture the places the characters are in your head.<br /><br />Interview:<br />Me: How did you feel about the days repeating?<br /><br />Amanda: I got really frustrated when everything came back day after day. Even the things I didn't want, like wearing a horrible itchy costume. I felt like I was the only person who saw that the days were repeating until I noticed Leo who was acting different every day. Then, I figured out it was his birthday and wondered was it something to do with that.<br /><br />Me: What was one thing that you learned from this?<br /><br />Amanda: I learned that even though you may be in a fight with your friend, you can't give up on each other, you have to get over it at one point, and talk it out.<br /><br />Me: How did you feel when you and Leo got to be friends again?<br /><br />Amanda: It felt really good to have someone that you knew forever back into your life. It made me feel so proud even though we had to go through days repeating. All that matters is that we are back together and found how to work it out.</span>

<div id="review_1192572124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192572124" />
    <a title="Isabella Schmitz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37036659-isabella-schmitz"><img alt="Isabella Schmitz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422979971p2/37036659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192572124?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabella Schmitz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabella Schmitz" href="/user/show/37036659-isabella-schmitz">Isabella Schmitz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192572124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer573069979797579764">11 Birthdays by: Wendy Mass is a fun, creative, full of friendship, mysterious and downright exciting book.<br/><br/>Amanda is an average girl living in an average town (Willow Falls) with an average best friend, well USED to be best friend. Amanda and Leo have the same birthday and ever since they were one they have shared it together and have been best friends. However on their 10th birthday Leo learns that their are words that you can never take back. It is the night of their 11th birthday and the nigh</span>
  <span id="freeText573069979797579764" style="display:none">11 Birthdays by: Wendy Mass is a fun, creative, full of friendship, mysterious and downright exciting book.<br /><br />Amanda is an average girl living in an average town (Willow Falls) with an average best friend, well USED to be best friend. Amanda and Leo have the same birthday and ever since they were one they have shared it together and have been best friends. However on their 10th birthday Leo learns that their are words that you can never take back. It is the night of their 11th birthday and the night of the 1st birthday they haven't shared together AND the night of the one year anniversary of not being friends. Amanda wakes up to a birthday full of pop quizzes, broken lockers, lost jobs, itchy costumes and scary Sponge Bob balloons. Amanda can't wait to wake up the next day and for it to be the weekend. Their is only one thing holding Amanda back from having a great Saturday. It's her and Leo's birthday all over again, but she and Leo are the only ones that realize it. Together Amanda and Leo have to solve this strange mystery.<br /><br />This book would fit into the genre of mystery because Amanda and Leo have no idea why this is happening and they have to work together to solve this mystery. I really like this book. It is a really good book to read for pleasure and enjoyment. And I definitely found both pleasure and enjoyment in reading 11 Birthdays. My favorite part in this book is when Leo and Amanda find out how to break their ever-repeating birthday. I am able to connect with Amanda and feel her happiness and sense of accomplishment which I really enjoy. I find that when I am reading this book I am able to become sucked into it. When Amanda feels frustrated that it is her birthday AGAIN I am there feeling frustrated with her. I really enjoy Wendy Mass's writing style, especially the specific details that she brings up again and again to emphasize that this is an important part or a key idea in the story or that this represents something. For example the birth mark and the Sponge Bob balloon are two examples from the text about again and again. <br /><br />I loved this book and I know that if you like silly books or mystery books or books full of friendship or downright exciting books or all these genres, this is a book for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="573069979797579764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194456421" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194456421?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/5164037-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194456421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14201738005149522511">Amanda and Leo, born on the same day, have celebrated their birthdays together for 10 years. Still feeling hurt from an unkind remark Leo made at last year’s party, Amanda spends her eleventh birthday without her now-estranged friend to share the fun. In the days that follow, both Amanda and Leo discover that they are caught in a time loop, waking up each morning to find themselves repeating their eleventh birthdays. They soon renew their friendship and begin to experiment by making different ch</span>
  <span id="freeText14201738005149522511" style="display:none">Amanda and Leo, born on the same day, have celebrated their birthdays together for 10 years. Still feeling hurt from an unkind remark Leo made at last year’s party, Amanda spends her eleventh birthday without her now-estranged friend to share the fun. In the days that follow, both Amanda and Leo discover that they are caught in a time loop, waking up each morning to find themselves repeating their eleventh birthdays. They soon renew their friendship and begin to experiment by making different choices throughout the day, partly for the thrill of acting without long-term consequences and partly from their fear of never escaping this mysterious time trap. From the double-entendre title to the solid character portrayals to the clarity and wit of the writing, this novel offers a fresh twist on the familiar themes of middle-grade family and school dynamics. The mysterious power that rewinds time eventually seems less important than the power that Amanda finds within herself. Emboldened by the idea of daily do-overs, she discovers that small changes in her attitude and actions result in sometimes-subtle, sometimes-monumental shifts in results for herself, her family, and her friends. A book for young readers but a fun one that I can't wait to pass on to my Nieces.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14201738005149522511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText18044705580348109149" style="display:none">11 birthdays is a book that children will LITERALLY fall in love with. this book represents and encourages friendship between Leo Fizpatrick,and Amanda Ellbery, two kids who were born on the same day, and were best friends until some "misunderstandings." when i read it, i couldn't put it down. i know other kids like me will enjoy it as much as i did. <br /><br />Best friends Leo and Amanda search for answers when the day of their 11TH birthdays repeat constantly.<br />they want answers quick. it all falls to the woman with the duck shaped birthmark that wiggled when she spoke. the two kids go on a quest (but not a faraway kind of quest) to find out why the awful 11TH <br />birthday day is repeating. when the pieces are put together, it is the friendship they are missing. <br />Many flash backs come to 11 birthdays, some when they were born. it all shows then together. no matter HOW hard they try, they become from best friends, to rivals (at least according to Amanda), to BEST BEST BEST friends again.<br /><br />Wendy Mass has shown a lesson and friendship in this story. Lesson: Friendship follows everywhere. Even between rivals and enemies. Wendy Mass has done it again, making me smile on even one of my worst days.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer212630426" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14246384055820484324">Imagine living the same day over and over and no one knowing it but yourself.... That's what is happening to Amanda Ellerby on her 11th birthday. She keeps waking up and it's the morning of her 11th birthday, but she already knows how the day is going to turn out - she'll get in a fight with her older sister, her dad will be too sick to help with her birthday party, her mom will lose her job that night, she'll have to try out for the gymnastics team just because her best friend wants her to, and</span>
  <span id="freeText14246384055820484324" style="display:none">Imagine living the same day over and over and no one knowing it but yourself.... That's what is happening to Amanda Ellerby on her 11th birthday. She keeps waking up and it's the morning of her 11th birthday, but she already knows how the day is going to turn out - she'll get in a fight with her older sister, her dad will be too sick to help with her birthday party, her mom will lose her job that night, she'll have to try out for the gymnastics team just because her best friend wants her to, and worst of all, she'll have to relive her miserable birthday party where no one really wants to be there because they want to be at her classmate, Leo's, party. And the hardest part of that, Leo used to be her best friend until their 10th birthday party. Could this have something to do with their fight from a year ago?<br />Fourth graders will enjoy this book and mature 3rd grade readers will, as well. Even though you keep reliving the same day over and over with Amanda, the little discoveries she makes each day keep you going! I like how Amanda learned something about herself each day.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7306252102767577336">I currently finished 11 Birthdays by Wendy Mass. This book starts with Amanda on her 11th birthday. She's not enjoying it like she has in the past. For her this was a different birthday, for the first time she and her best friend Leo weren't having their parties together. All the information author gives away about that is that they haven't spoken in a year. When I read this I was thinking why are they not talking and what caused them not to speak to each other? I was excited to figure out what </span>
  <span id="freeText7306252102767577336" style="display:none">I currently finished 11 Birthdays by Wendy Mass. This book starts with Amanda on her 11th birthday. She's not enjoying it like she has in the past. For her this was a different birthday, for the first time she and her best friend Leo weren't having their parties together. All the information author gives away about that is that they haven't spoken in a year. When I read this I was thinking why are they not talking and what caused them not to speak to each other? I was excited to figure out what happened next and how it affected the characters. All Amanda can do wait for the next day to come. But when she wakes up to everything being same as the day before things get really strange. She and Leo have to forget about their past and learn about true friendship and teamwork to break their repeating birthdays. I can make a connection to Amanda because everyone has friendship troubles and fights. But in the end everything is back to normal and just as before. I enjoy this book and recommend it to anyone who likes realistic fiction with a little fantasy. This book is really a Good Read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7306252102767577336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JsJy6A54GqD9AU5uebGoAoonec33kbEwu9vL9R1T9L0ajkQ7/Y5c1XN8RmbZl7nS2/56jXUtjKhhl9GudPzfog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZS+NEtIupgUhbqPlEFYrbkjV9TsD5StlnuiGLb3zsIhZY7vBIdjgcK8Tq+2wcDq+GQz2e4FZFv1EpJx21Fyblw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18179421367351752469">Wendy Mass is the author of twenty-two novels for young people, including A Mango-Shaped Space, which was awarded the Schneider Family Book Award, Leap Day, the Twice Upon a Time fairy tale series, Jeremy Fink and the Meaning of Life, Heaven Looks a Lot Like the Mall, the Willow Falls, Space Taxi and Candymakers series. Wendy wrote the storyline for an episode of the television show Monk, entitled</span>
  <span id="freeText18179421367351752469" style="display:none">Wendy Mass is the author of twenty-two novels for young people, including A Mango-Shaped Space, which was awarded the Schneider Family Book Award, Leap Day, the Twice Upon a Time fairy tale series, Jeremy Fink and the Meaning of Life, Heaven Looks a Lot Like the Mall, the Willow Falls, Space Taxi and Candymakers series. Wendy wrote the storyline for an episode of the television show Monk, entitled "Mr. Monk Goes to the Theatre," which aired during the show's second season. She tells people her hobbies are hiking and photography, but really they're collecting candy bar wrappers and searching for buried treasure with her metal detector. Wendy lives with her family in New Jersey.</span>
